        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A restartable version of the S-IVB was used as the third stage of the Saturn V. The Saturn IB could send over 40,000 pounds (18,100 kg) into low Earth orbit, sufficient for a partially fueled CSM or the LM.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Saturn IB launch vehicles and flights were designated with an AS-200 series number, "AS" indicating "Apollo Saturn" and the "2" indicating the second member of the Saturn rocket family.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Origin_of_NASA's_Names_60-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Origin_of_NASA's_Names-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Saturn_V">
        Saturn V
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Saturn V">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Saturn_V" title="Saturn V">
        Saturn V
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_11_Saturn_V_lifting_off_on_July_16,_1969.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2862" data-file-width="2280" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Apollo_11_Saturn_V_lifting_off_on_July_16%2C_1969.jpg/150px-Apollo_11_Saturn_V_lifting_off_on_July_16%2C_1969.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Apollo_11_Saturn_V_lifting_off_on_July_16%2C_1969.jpg/225px-Apollo_11_Saturn_V_lifting_off_on_July_16%2C_1969.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Apollo_11_Saturn_V_lifting_off_on_July_16%2C_1969.jpg/300px-Apollo_11_Saturn_V_lifting_off_on_July_16%2C_1969.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_11_Saturn_V_lifting_off_on_July_16,_1969.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A Saturn V launches Apollo 11 in 1969
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Saturn V launch vehicles and flights were designated with an AS-500 series number, "AS" indicating "Apollo Saturn" and the "5" indicating Saturn V.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Origin_of_NASA's_Names_60-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Origin_of_NASA's_Names-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The three-stage Saturn V was designed to send a fully fueled CSM and LM to the Moon. It was 33 feet (10.1 m) in diameter and stood 363 feet (110.6 m) tall with its 96,800-pound (43,900 kg) lunar payload. Its capability grew to 103,600 pounds (47,000 kg) for the later advanced lunar landings. The
       <a href="/wiki/S-IC" title="S-IC">
        S-IC
       </a>
       first stage burned RP-1/LOX for a rated thrust of 7,500,000 pounds-force (33,400 kN), which was upgraded to 7,610,000 pounds-force (33,900 kN). The second and third stages burned liquid hydrogen, and the third stage was a modified version of the S-IVB, with thrust increased to 230,000 pounds-force (1,020 kN) and capability to restart the engine for translunar injection after reaching a
       <a href="/wiki/Parking_orbit" title="Parking orbit">
        parking orbit
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABTN_LV1_61-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ABTN_LV1-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Astronauts">
        Astronauts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Astronauts">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Apollo_astronauts" title="List of Apollo astronauts">
        List of Apollo astronauts
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_1_Prime_Crew_-_GPN-2000-001159.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3000" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Apollo_1_Prime_Crew_-_GPN-2000-001159.jpg/220px-Apollo_1_Prime_Crew_-_GPN-2000-001159.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Apollo_1_Prime_Crew_-_GPN-2000-001159.jpg/330px-Apollo_1_Prime_Crew_-_GPN-2000-001159.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Apollo_1_Prime_Crew_-_GPN-2000-001159.jpg/440px-Apollo_1_Prime_Crew_-_GPN-2000-001159.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_1_Prime_Crew_-_GPN-2000-001159.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_1" title="Apollo 1">
          Apollo 1
         </a>
         crew:
         <a href="/wiki/Ed_White_(astronaut)" title="Ed White (astronaut)">
          Ed White
         </a>
         , command pilot
         <a href="/wiki/Gus_Grissom" title="Gus Grissom">
          Gus Grissom
         </a>
         , and
         <a href="/wiki/Roger_B._Chaffee" title="Roger B. Chaffee">
          Roger Chaffee
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       NASA's Director of Flight Crew Operations during the Apollo program was
       <a href="/wiki/Deke_Slayton" title="Deke Slayton">
        Donald K. "Deke" Slayton
       </a>
       , one of the original
       <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Seven" title="Mercury Seven">
        Mercury Seven
       </a>
       astronauts who was medically grounded in September 1962 due to a
       <a href="/wiki/Heart_murmur" title="Heart murmur">
        heart murmur
       </a>
       . Slayton was responsible for making all Gemini and Apollo crew assignments.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_11.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3300" data-file-width="4200" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Apollo_11.jpg/220px-Apollo_11.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Apollo_11.jpg/330px-Apollo_11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Apollo_11.jpg/440px-Apollo_11.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_11.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Apollo 11 crew, who made the first manned landing: commander
         <a href="/wiki/Neil_Armstrong" title="Neil Armstrong">
          Neil Armstrong
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Command/Service_Module#Command_Module_(CM)" title="Apollo Command/Service Module">
          CM
         </a>
         pilot
         <a href="/wiki/Michael_Collins_(astronaut)" title="Michael Collins (astronaut)">
          Michael Collins
         </a>
         , and LM pilot
         <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Aldrin" title="Buzz Aldrin">
          Buzz Aldrin
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Thirty-two astronauts were assigned to fly missions in the Apollo program. Twenty-four of these left Earth’s orbit and flew around the Moon between December 1968 and December 1972 (three of them twice). Half of the 24 walked on its surface, though none of them returned to the Moon after landing once. One of the moonwalkers was a trained geologist. Of the 32,
       <a href="/wiki/Gus_Grissom" title="Gus Grissom">
        Gus Grissom
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ed_White_(astronaut)" title="Ed White (astronaut)">
        Ed White
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Roger_B._Chaffee" title="Roger B. Chaffee">
        Roger Chaffee
       </a>
       were killed during a ground test in preparation for their Apollo 1 mission.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-missionNumbers_53-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-missionNumbers-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Apollo astronauts were chosen from the Project Mercury and Gemini veterans, plus from two later astronaut groups. All missions were commanded by Gemini or Mercury veterans. Crews on all development flights (except the Earth orbit CSM development flights) through the first two landings on Apollo 11 and
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_12" title="Apollo 12">
        Apollo 12
       </a>
       , included at least two (sometimes three) Gemini veterans. Dr.
       <a href="/wiki/Harrison_Schmitt" title="Harrison Schmitt">
        Harrison Schmitt
       </a>
       , a geologist, was the first
       <a href="/wiki/NASA_Astronaut_Group_4" title="NASA Astronaut Group 4">
        NASA scientist astronaut
       </a>
       to fly in space, and landed on the Moon on the last mission, Apollo 17. Schmitt participated in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geology_of_the_moon" title="Geology of the moon">
        lunar geology
       </a>
       training of all of the Apollo landing crews.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       NASA awarded all 32 of these astronauts its highest honor, the
       <a href="/wiki/NASA_Distinguished_Service_Medal" title="NASA Distinguished Service Medal">
        Distinguished Service Medal
       </a>
       , given for "distinguished service, ability, or courage", and personal "contribution representing substantial progress to the NASA mission". The medals were awarded posthumously to Grissom, White, and Chaffee in 1969, then to the crews of all missions from
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_8" title="Apollo 8">
        Apollo 8
       </a>
       onward. The crew that flew the first Earth orbital test mission
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_7" title="Apollo 7">
        Apollo 7
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wally_Schirra" title="Wally Schirra">
        Walter M. Schirra
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Donn_Eisele" title="Donn Eisele">
        Donn Eisele
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Walter_Cunningham" title="Walter Cunningham">
        Walter Cunningham
       </a>
       , were awarded the lesser
       <a href="/wiki/NASA_Exceptional_Service_Medal" title="NASA Exceptional Service Medal">
        NASA Exceptional Service Medal
       </a>
       , because of discipline problems with the
       <a href="/wiki/Flight_controller#Flight_Director_(FLIGHT)" title="Flight controller">
        Flight Director
       </a>
       's orders during their flight. The NASA Administrator in October, 2008, decided to award them the Distinguished Service Medals, by this time posthumously to Schirra and Eisele.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Apollo_Crew_Honored_2008_64-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Apollo_Crew_Honored_2008-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Lunar_mission_profile">
        Lunar mission profile
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Lunar mission profile">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The nominal planned lunar landing mission proceeded as follows:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 225px">
        <div style="width: 225px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 220px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo11-01.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="760" data-file-width="1103" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Apollo11-01.png/190px-Apollo11-01.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Apollo11-01.png/285px-Apollo11-01.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Apollo11-01.png/380px-Apollo11-01.png 2x" width="190"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <b>
            Launch
           </b>
           The 3 Saturn V stages burn for about 11 minutes to achieve a 100-nautical-mile (190 km) circular
           <a href="/wiki/Parking_orbit" title="Parking orbit">
            parking orbit
           </a>
           . The third stage burns a small portion of its fuel to achieve orbit.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 225px">
        <div style="width: 225px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 220px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo11-02.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="808" data-file-width="1172" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Apollo11-02.png/190px-Apollo11-02.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Apollo11-02.png/285px-Apollo11-02.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Apollo11-02.png/380px-Apollo11-02.png 2x" width="190"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <b>
            <a href="/wiki/Trans-lunar_injection" title="Trans-lunar injection">
             Translunar injection
            </a>
           </b>
           After one to two orbits to verify readiness of spacecraft systems, the
           <a href="/wiki/S-IVB" title="S-IVB">
            S-IVB
           </a>
           third stage reignites for about 6 minutes to send the spacecraft to the Moon.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 225px">
        <div style="width: 225px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 220px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo11-03.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="749" data-file-width="1086" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Apollo11-03.png/190px-Apollo11-03.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Apollo11-03.png/285px-Apollo11-03.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Apollo11-03.png/380px-Apollo11-03.png 2x" width="190"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <b>
            <a href="/wiki/Transposition,_docking,_and_extraction" title="Transposition, docking, and extraction">
             Transposition and docking
            </a>
            (1)
           </b>
           The
           <a href="/wiki/Apollo_(spacecraft)#Spacecraft_Lunar_Module_Adapter_(SLA)" title="Apollo (spacecraft)">
            Spacecraft Lunar Module Adapter
           </a>
           (SLA) panels separate to free the CSM and expose the LM. The Command Module Pilot (CMP) moves the CSM out a safe distance, and turns 180°.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 225px">
        <div style="width: 225px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 220px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo11-04.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="870" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Apollo11-04.png/190px-Apollo11-04.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Apollo11-04.png/285px-Apollo11-04.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Apollo11-04.png/380px-Apollo11-04.png 2x" width="190"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <b>
            Transposition and docking (2)
           </b>
           , The CMP docks with the LM, and pulls the combined spacecraft away from the S-IVB, which then is sent into solar orbit. The lunar voyage takes between 2 and 3 days. Midcourse corrections are made as necessary using the
           <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Command/Service_Module#Service_Module_(SM)" title="Apollo Command/Service Module">
            SM
           </a>
           engine.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 225px">
        <div style="width: 225px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 220px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo11-05.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="610" data-file-width="884" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Apollo11-05.png/190px-Apollo11-05.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Apollo11-05.png/285px-Apollo11-05.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Apollo11-05.png/380px-Apollo11-05.png 2x" width="190"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <b>
            <a href="/wiki/Lunar_orbit" title="Lunar orbit">
             Lunar orbit
            </a>
            insertion
           </b>
           The spacecraft passes about 60 nautical miles (110 km) behind the Moon, and the SM engine is fired to slow the spacecraft and put it into a 60-by-170-nautical-mile (110 by 310 km) orbit, which is soon circularized at 60 nautical miles by a second burn.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 225px">
        <div style="width: 225px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 220px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo11-07.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="626" data-file-width="908" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Apollo11-07.png/190px-Apollo11-07.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Apollo11-07.png/285px-Apollo11-07.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Apollo11-07.png/380px-Apollo11-07.png 2x" width="190"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           After a rest period, the Commander (CDR) and Lunar Module Pilot (LMP) move to the LM, power up its systems, and deploy the landing gear. The CSM and LM separate; the CMP visually inspects the LM, then the LM crew move a safe distance away and fire the descent engine for
           <b>
            Descent orbit insertion
           </b>
           , which takes it to a
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perilune" title="Perilune">
            perilune
           </a>
           of about 50,000 feet (15 km).
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 225px">
        <div style="width: 225px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 220px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo11-08.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="822" data-file-width="1192" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Apollo11-08.png/190px-Apollo11-08.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Apollo11-08.png/285px-Apollo11-08.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Apollo11-08.png/380px-Apollo11-08.png 2x" width="190"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <b>
            <a href="/wiki/Powered_Descent_Initiation" title="Powered Descent Initiation">
             Powered descent
            </a>
           </b>
           At perilune, the descent engine fires again to start the descent. The CDR takes over manual control after pitchover for a vertical landing.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 225px">
        <div style="width: 225px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 220px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo11-09.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="769" data-file-width="1115" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Apollo11-09.png/190px-Apollo11-09.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Apollo11-09.png/285px-Apollo11-09.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Apollo11-09.png/380px-Apollo11-09.png 2x" width="190"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           The CDR and LMP perform one or more
           <a href="/wiki/Extravehicular_activity" title="Extravehicular activity">
            EVAs
           </a>
           exploring the lunar surface and collecting samples, alternating with rest periods.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 225px">
        <div style="width: 225px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 220px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo11-10.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="845" data-file-width="1225" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Apollo11-10.png/190px-Apollo11-10.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Apollo11-10.png/285px-Apollo11-10.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Apollo11-10.png/380px-Apollo11-10.png 2x" width="190"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           The
           <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Module#Ascent_stage" title="Apollo Lunar Module">
            ascent stage
           </a>
           lifts off, using the descent stage as a launching pad.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 225px">
        <div style="width: 225px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 220px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo11-11.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="820" data-file-width="1189" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Apollo11-11.png/190px-Apollo11-11.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Apollo11-11.png/285px-Apollo11-11.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Apollo11-11.png/380px-Apollo11-11.png 2x" width="190"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           The LM rendezvouses and docks with the CSM.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 225px">
        <div style="width: 225px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 220px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo11-12.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="671" data-file-width="973" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Apollo11-12.png/190px-Apollo11-12.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Apollo11-12.png/285px-Apollo11-12.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Apollo11-12.png/380px-Apollo11-12.png 2x" width="190"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           The CDR and LMP transfer back to the CM with their material samples, then the LM ascent stage is jettisoned, to eventually fall out of orbit and crash on the surface.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 225px">
        <div style="width: 225px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 220px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo11-13.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="652" data-file-width="946" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Apollo11-13.png/190px-Apollo11-13.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Apollo11-13.png/285px-Apollo11-13.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Apollo11-13.png/380px-Apollo11-13.png 2x" width="190"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <b>
            <a href="/wiki/Trans-Earth_injection" title="Trans-Earth injection">
             Trans-Earth injection
            </a>
           </b>
           The SM engine fires to send the CSM back to Earth.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 225px">
        <div style="width: 225px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 220px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo11-14.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="452" data-file-width="656" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Apollo11-14.png/190px-Apollo11-14.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Apollo11-14.png/285px-Apollo11-14.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Apollo11-14.png/380px-Apollo11-14.png 2x" width="190"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           The SM is jettisoned just before reentry, and the CM turns 180° to face its blunt end forward for reentry.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 225px">
        <div style="width: 225px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 220px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo11-15.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="899" data-file-width="1303" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Apollo11-15.png/190px-Apollo11-15.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Apollo11-15.png/285px-Apollo11-15.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Apollo11-15.png/380px-Apollo11-15.png 2x" width="190"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           Atmospheric drag slows the CM. Aerodynamic heating surrounds it with an envelope of ionized air which causes a communications blackout for several minutes.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 225px">
        <div style="width: 225px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 220px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo11-16.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="889" data-file-width="1289" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Apollo11-16.png/190px-Apollo11-16.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Apollo11-16.png/285px-Apollo11-16.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Apollo11-16.png/380px-Apollo11-16.png 2x" width="190"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           Parachutes are deployed, slowing the CM for a splashdown in the
           <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
            Pacific Ocean
           </a>
           . The astronauts are recovered and brought to an
           <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">
            aircraft carrier
           </a>
           .
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 505px">
        <div style="width: 505px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 500px;">
          <div style="margin:15.5px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo-Moon-mission-profile.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="603" data-file-width="965" height="294" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Apollo-Moon-mission-profile.png/470px-Apollo-Moon-mission-profile.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Apollo-Moon-mission-profile.png/705px-Apollo-Moon-mission-profile.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Apollo-Moon-mission-profile.png/940px-Apollo-Moon-mission-profile.png 2x" width="470"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           Lunar flight profile (distances not to scale).
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Profile_variations">
        Profile variations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Profile variations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Starting with Apollo 13, descent orbit insertion was to be performed using the Service Module engine instead of the LM engine, in order to allow a greater fuel reserve for landing. This was actually done for the first time on Apollo 14, since the Apollo 13 mission was aborted before landing.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
         <a href="#cite_note-66">
          [66]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        The first three lunar missions (Apollo 8,
        <a href="/wiki/Apollo_10" title="Apollo 10">
         Apollo 10
        </a>
        , and Apollo 11) used a
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_return_trajectory" title="Free return trajectory">
         free return trajectory
        </a>
        , keeping a flight path coplanar with the lunar orbit, which would allow a return to Earth in case the SM engine failed to make lunar orbit insertion. Landing site lighting conditions on later missions dictated a lunar orbital plane change, which required a course change maneuver soon after TLI, and eliminated the free-return option.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
         <a href="#cite_note-67">
          [67]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        After Apollo 12 placed the second of several
        <a href="/wiki/Seismometer" title="Seismometer">
         seismometers
        </a>
        on the Moon,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
         <a href="#cite_note-68">
          [68]
         </a>
        </sup>
        the S-IVBs on subsequent missions were deliberately crashed on the Moon instead of being sent to solar orbit, as an active seismic experiment to induce vibrations in the Moon.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
         <a href="#cite_note-69">
          [69]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        As another active seismic experiment, the jettisoned LM ascent stages on Apollo 12 and later missions were deliberately crashed on the Moon at known locations. The only exceptions to this were the Apollo 13 LM which burned up in the Earth's atmosphere, and
        <a href="/wiki/Apollo_16" title="Apollo 16">
         Apollo 16
        </a>
        , where a loss of
        <a href="/wiki/Attitude_control" title="Attitude control">
         attitude control
        </a>
        after jettison prevented making a targeted impact.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
         <a href="#cite_note-70">
          [70]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Development_history">
        Development history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Development history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Unmanned_flight_tests">
        Unmanned flight tests
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Unmanned flight tests">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <div class="noresize">
         <map id="ImageMap_1_73068706" name="ImageMap_1_73068706">
          <area alt="AS-201 first unmanned CSM test" coords="0,0,46,247" href="/wiki/AS-201" shape="rect" title="AS-201 first unmanned CSM test"/>
          <area alt="AS-203 S-IVB stage development test" coords="46,0,91,247" href="/wiki/AS-203" shape="rect" title="AS-203 S-IVB stage development test"/>
          <area alt="AS-202 second unmanned CSM test" coords="91,0,135,247" href="/wiki/AS-202" shape="rect" title="AS-202 second unmanned CSM test"/>
          <area alt="Apollo 4 first unmanned Saturn V test" coords="136,0,170,247" href="/wiki/Apollo_4" shape="rect" title="Apollo 4 first unmanned Saturn V test"/>
          <area alt="Apollo 5 unmanned LM test" coords="171,0,217,247" href="/wiki/Apollo_5" shape="rect" title="Apollo 5 unmanned LM test"/>
          <area alt="Apollo 6 second unmanned Saturn V test" coords="218,0,247,247" href="/wiki/Apollo_6" shape="rect" title="Apollo 6 second unmanned Saturn V test"/>
         </map>
         <img alt="Composite image of unmanned development Apollo mission launches in chronological sequence." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="491" data-file-width="500" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Apollo_unmanned_launches.png/250px-Apollo_unmanned_launches.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Apollo_unmanned_launches.png/375px-Apollo_unmanned_launches.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Apollo_unmanned_launches.png 2x" usemap="#ImageMap_1_73068706" width="250"/>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_unmanned_launches.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Apollo unmanned development mission launches. Click on a launch image to read the main article about each mission
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Apollo_missions" title="List of Apollo missions">
        List of Apollo missions
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Two Block I CSMs were launched from LC-34 on suborbital flights in 1966 with the Saturn IB. The first,
       <a href="/wiki/AS-201" title="AS-201">
        AS-201
       </a>
       launched on February 26, reached an altitude of 265.7 nautical miles (492.1 km) and splashed down 4,577 nautical miles (8,477 km) downrange in the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
        Atlantic Ocean
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The second,
       <a href="/wiki/AS-202" title="AS-202">
        AS-202
       </a>
       on August 25, reached 617.1 nautical miles (1,142.9 km) altitude and was recovered 13,900 nautical miles (25,700 km) downrange in the Pacific Ocean. These flights validated the Service Module engine and the Command Module heat shield.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A third Saturn IB test,
       <a href="/wiki/AS-203" title="AS-203">
        AS-203
       </a>
       launched from pad 37, went into orbit to support design of the S-IVB upper stage restart capability needed for the Saturn V. It carried a nosecone instead of the Apollo spacecraft, and its payload was the unburned liquid hydrogen fuel, the behavior of which engineers measured with temperature and pressure sensors, and a TV camera. This flight occurred on July 5, before AS-202, which was delayed because of problems getting the Apollo spacecraft ready for flight.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAreport_73-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NASAreport-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Preparation_for_manned_flight">
        Preparation for manned flight
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Preparation for manned flight">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Two manned orbital Block I CSM missions were planned: AS-204 and AS-205. The Block I crew positions were titled Command Pilot, Senior Pilot, and Pilot. The Senior Pilot would assume navigation duties, while the Pilot would function as a systems engineer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The astronauts would wear
       <a href="/wiki/Gemini_space_suit#Apollo_program" title="Gemini space suit">
        a modified version of the Gemini spacesuit
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After an unmanned LM test flight AS-206, a crew would fly the first Block II CSM and LM in a dual mission known as AS-207/208, or AS-278 (each spacecraft would be launched on a separate Saturn IB).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chariots8-5_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-chariots8-5-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Block II crew positions were titled Commander (CDR) Command Module Pilot (CMP) and Lunar Module Pilot (LMP). The astronauts would begin wearing a new
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo/Skylab_A7L" title="Apollo/Skylab A7L">
        Apollo A6L spacesuit
       </a>
       , designed to accommodate lunar
       <a href="/wiki/Extravehicular_activity" title="Extravehicular activity">
        extravehicular activity
       </a>
       (EVA). The traditional visor helmet was replaced with a clear "fishbowl" type for greater visibility, and the lunar surface EVA suit would include a water-cooled undergarment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EMU_development_77-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EMU_development-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Deke_Slayton" title="Deke Slayton">
        Deke Slayton
       </a>
       , the grounded
       <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Seven" title="Mercury Seven">
        Mercury astronaut
       </a>
       who became Director of Flight Crew Operations for the Gemini and Apollo programs, selected the first Apollo crew in January 1966, with Grissom as Command Pilot, White as Senior Pilot, and rookie
       <a href="/wiki/Donn_F._Eisele" title="Donn F. Eisele">
        Donn F. Eisele
       </a>
       as Pilot. But Eisele dislocated his shoulder twice aboard the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reduced_gravity_aircraft" title="Reduced gravity aircraft">
        KC135 weightlessness training aircraft
       </a>
       , and had to undergo surgery on January 27. Slayton replaced him with Chaffee.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whatshisname_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-whatshisname-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       NASA announced the final crew selection for AS-204 on March 21, 1966, with the backup crew consisting of Gemini veterans
       <a href="/wiki/James_McDivitt" title="James McDivitt">
        James McDivitt
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/David_Scott" title="David Scott">
        David Scott
       </a>
       , with rookie
       <a href="/wiki/Rusty_Schweickart" title="Rusty Schweickart">
        Russell L. "Rusty" Schweickart
       </a>
       . Mercury/Gemini veteran
       <a href="/wiki/Wally_Schirra" title="Wally Schirra">
        Wally Schirra
       </a>
       , Eisele, and rookie
       <a href="/wiki/Walter_Cunningham" title="Walter Cunningham">
        Walter Cunningham
       </a>
       were announced on September 29 as the prime crew for AS-205.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whatshisname_78-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-whatshisname-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In December 1966, the AS-205 mission was canceled, since the validation of the CSM would be accomplished on the 14-day first flight, and AS-205 would have been devoted to space experiments and contribute no new engineering knowledge about the spacecraft. Its Saturn IB was allocated to the dual mission, now redesignated AS-205/208 or AS-258, planned for August 1967. McDivitt, Scott and Schweickart were promoted to the prime AS-258 crew, and Schirra, Eisele and Cunningham were reassigned as the Apollo 1 backup crew.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Program_delays">
        Program delays
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Program delays">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The spacecraft for the AS-202 and AS-204 missions were delivered by North American Aviation to the Kennedy Space Center with long lists of equipment problems which had to be corrected before flight; these delays caused the launch of AS-202 to slip behind AS-203, and eliminated hopes the first manned mission might be ready to launch as soon as November 1966, concurrently with the last Gemini mission. Eventually the planned AS-204 flight date was pushed to February 21, 1967.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SP4029_80-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SP4029-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       North American Aviation was prime contractor not only for the Apollo CSM, but for the Saturn V
       <a href="/wiki/S-II" title="S-II">
        S-II
       </a>
       second stage as well, and delays in this stage pushed the first unmanned Saturn V flight AS-501 from late 1966 to November 1967. (The initial assembly of AS-501 had to use a dummy spacer spool in place of the stage.)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The problems with North American were severe enough in late 1965 to cause Manned Space Flight Administrator George Mueller to appoint program director Samuel Phillips to head a "
       <a href="/wiki/Tiger_team" title="Tiger team">
        tiger team
       </a>
       " to investigate North American's problems and identify corrections. Phillips documented his findings in a December 19 letter to NAA president
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lee_Atwood" title="Lee Atwood">
        Lee Atwood
       </a>
       , with a strongly worded letter by Mueller, and also gave a presentation of the results to Mueller and Deputy Administrator Robert Seamans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Meanwhile,
       <a href="/wiki/Grumman" title="Grumman">
        Grumman
       </a>
       was also encountering problems with the Lunar Module, eliminating hopes it would be ready for manned flight in 1967, not long after the first manned CSM flights.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Apollo_1_fire">
        Apollo 1 fire
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Apollo 1 fire">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_1" title="Apollo 1">
        Apollo 1
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_1_fire.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2702" data-file-width="4000" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Apollo_1_fire.jpg/220px-Apollo_1_fire.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Apollo_1_fire.jpg/330px-Apollo_1_fire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Apollo_1_fire.jpg/440px-Apollo_1_fire.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_1_fire.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Charred Apollo 1 cabin interior
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Grissom, White, and Chaffee decided to name their flight Apollo 1 as a motivational focus on the first manned flight. They trained and conducted tests of their spacecraft at North American, and in the altitude chamber at the Kennedy Space Center. A "plugs-out" test was planned for January, which would simulate a launch countdown on LC-34 with the spacecraft transferring from pad-supplied to internal power. If successful, this would be followed by a more rigorous countdown simulation test closer to the February 21 launch, with both spacecraft and launch vehicle fueled.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sea4_84-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-sea4-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The plugs-out test began on the morning of January 27, 1967, and immediately was plagued with problems. First the crew noticed a strange odor in their spacesuits, which delayed the sealing of the hatch. Then, communications problems frustrated the astronauts and forced a hold in the simulated countdown. During this hold, an electrical fire began in the cabin, and spread quickly in the high pressure, 100% oxygen atmosphere. Pressure rose high enough from the fire that the cabin inner wall burst, allowing the fire to erupt onto the pad area and frustrating attempts to rescue the crew. The astronauts were asphyxiated before the hatch could be opened.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sea5_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-sea5-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       NASA immediately convened an accident review board, overseen by both houses of Congress. While the determination of responsibility for the accident was complex, the review board concluded that "deficiencies existed in Command Module design, workmanship and quality control."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sea5_85-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-sea5-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At the insistence of NASA Administrator Webb, North American removed
       <a href="/wiki/Harrison_Storms" title="Harrison Storms">
        Harrison Storms
       </a>
       as Command Module program manager.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Webb also reassigned Apollo Spacecraft Program Office (ASPO) Manager
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Francis_Shea" title="Joseph Francis Shea">
        Joseph Francis Shea
       </a>
       , replacing him with
       <a href="/wiki/George_Low" title="George Low">
        George Low
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KeyPersonnelChange_87-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-KeyPersonnelChange-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Irwin_i_Bull_testuj%C4%85_kombinezony_kosmiczne_S68-15931.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="471" data-file-width="384" height="270" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Irwin_i_Bull_testuj%C4%85_kombinezony_kosmiczne_S68-15931.jpg/220px-Irwin_i_Bull_testuj%C4%85_kombinezony_kosmiczne_S68-15931.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Irwin_i_Bull_testuj%C4%85_kombinezony_kosmiczne_S68-15931.jpg/330px-Irwin_i_Bull_testuj%C4%85_kombinezony_kosmiczne_S68-15931.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/38/Irwin_i_Bull_testuj%C4%85_kombinezony_kosmiczne_S68-15931.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Irwin_i_Bull_testuj%C4%85_kombinezony_kosmiczne_S68-15931.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Block II spacesuit in January 1968, before (left) and after changes recommended after the Apollo 1 fire
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       To remedy the causes of the fire, changes were made in the Block II spacecraft and operational procedures, the most important of which were use of a nitrogen/oxygen mixture instead of pure oxygen before and during launch, and removal of flammable cabin and space suit materials.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chariot_88-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-chariot-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Block II design already called for replacement of the Block I
       <a href="/wiki/Plug_door" title="Plug door">
        plug-type
       </a>
       hatch cover with a quick-release, outward opening door.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chariot_88-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-chariot-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       NASA discontinued the manned Block I program, using the Block I spacecraft only for unmanned Saturn V flights. Crew members would also exclusively wear modified, fire-resistant A7L Block II space suits, and would be designated by the Block II titles, regardless of whether a LM was present on the flight or not.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EMU_development_77-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-EMU_development-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Unmanned_Saturn_V_and_LM_tests">
        Unmanned Saturn V and LM tests
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Unmanned Saturn V and LM tests">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       On April 24, 1967, Mueller published an official Apollo mission numbering scheme, using sequential numbers for all flights, manned or unmanned. The sequence would start with
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_4" title="Apollo 4">
        Apollo 4
       </a>
       to cover the first three unmanned flights while retiring the Apollo 1 designation to honor the crew, per their widows' wishes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-missionNumbers_53-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-missionNumbers-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In September 1967, Mueller approved a
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Apollo_mission_types" title="List of Apollo mission types">
        sequence of mission types
       </a>
       which had to be successfully accomplished in order to achieve the manned lunar landing. Each step had to be successfully accomplished before the next ones could be performed, and it was unknown how many tries of each mission would be necessary; therefore letters were used instead of numbers. The
       <b>
        A
       </b>
       missions were unmanned Saturn V validation;
       <b>
        B
       </b>
       was unmanned LM validation using the Saturn IB;
       <b>
        C
       </b>
       was manned CSM Earth orbit validation using the Saturn IB;
       <b>
        D
       </b>
       was the first manned CSM/LM flight (this replaced AS-258, using a single Saturn V launch);
       <b>
        E
       </b>
       would be a higher Earth orbit CSM/LM flight;
       <b>
        F
       </b>
       would be the first lunar mission, testing the LM in lunar orbit but without landing (a "dress rehearsal"); and
       <b>
        G
       </b>
       would be the first manned landing. The list of types covered follow-on lunar exploration to include
       <b>
        H
       </b>
       lunar landings,
       <b>
        I
       </b>
       for lunar orbital survey missions, and
       <b>
        J
       </b>
       for extended-stay lunar landings.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3Q1967_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-3Q1967-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The delay in the CSM caused by the fire enabled NASA to catch up on man-rating the LM and Saturn V. Apollo 4 (AS-501) was the first unmanned flight of the Saturn V, carrying a Block I CSM on November 9, 1967. The capability of the Command Module's heat shield to survive a trans-lunar reentry was demonstrated by using the Service Module engine to ram it into the atmosphere at higher than the usual Earth-orbital reentry speed.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_5" title="Apollo 5">
        Apollo 5
       </a>
       (AS-204) was the first unmanned test flight of LM in Earth orbit, launched from pad 37 on January 22, 1968, by the Saturn IB that would have been used for Apollo 1. The LM engines were successfully test-fired and restarted, despite a computer programming error which cut short the first descent stage firing. The ascent engine was fired in abort mode, known as a "fire-in-the-hole" test, where it was lit simultaneously with jettison of the descent stage. Although Grumman wanted a second unmanned test, George Low decided the next LM flight would be manned.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       This was followed on April 4, 1968, by
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_6" title="Apollo 6">
        Apollo 6
       </a>
       (AS-502) which carried a CSM and a LM Test Article as ballast. The intent of this mission was to achieve trans-lunar injection, followed closely by a simulated direct-return abort, using the Service Module engine to achieve another high-speed reentry. The Saturn V experienced
       <a href="/wiki/Pogo_oscillation" title="Pogo oscillation">
        pogo oscillation
       </a>
       , a problem caused by non-steady engine combustion, which damaged fuel lines in the second and third stages. Two S-II engines shut down prematurely, but the remaining engines were able to compensate. The damage to the third stage engine was more severe, preventing it from restarting for trans-lunar injection. Mission controllers were able to use the Service Module engine to essentially repeat the flight profile of Apollo 4. Based on the good performance of Apollo 6 and identification of satisfactory fixes to the Apollo 6 problems, NASA declared the Saturn V ready to fly men, cancelling a third unmanned test.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Manned_development_missions">
        Manned development missions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Manned development missions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <div class="noresize">
         <map id="ImageMap_2_1545928124" name="ImageMap_2_1545928124">
          <area alt="Apollo 1 unsuccessful first manned CSM test" coords="0,0,71,72" href="/wiki/Apollo_1" shape="rect" title="Apollo 1 unsuccessful first manned CSM test"/>
          <area alt="Apollo 7 first manned CSM test" coords="72,0,165,72" href="/wiki/Apollo_7" shape="rect" title="Apollo 7 first manned CSM test"/>
          <area alt="Apollo 8 first manned flight to the Moon" coords="165,0,249,72" href="/wiki/Apollo_8" shape="rect" title="Apollo 8 first manned flight to the Moon"/>
          <area alt="Apollo 9 manned Earth orbital LM test" coords="0,72,71,144" href="/wiki/Apollo_9" shape="rect" title="Apollo 9 manned Earth orbital LM test"/>
          <area alt="Apollo 10 manned lunar orbital LM test" coords="72,72,165,144" href="/wiki/Apollo_10" shape="rect" title="Apollo 10 manned lunar orbital LM test"/>
          <area alt="Apollo 11 first manned Moon landing" coords="165,72,249,144" href="/wiki/Apollo_11" shape="rect" title="Apollo 11 first manned Moon landing"/>
         </map>
         <img alt="Composite image of 6 manned Apollo development mission patches, from Apollo 1 to Apollo 11." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="2081" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Apollo_manned_development_missions_insignia.png/250px-Apollo_manned_development_missions_insignia.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Apollo_manned_development_missions_insignia.png/375px-Apollo_manned_development_missions_insignia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Apollo_manned_development_missions_insignia.png/500px-Apollo_manned_development_missions_insignia.png 2x" usemap="#ImageMap_2_1545928124" width="250"/>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_manned_development_missions_insignia.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Apollo manned development mission patches. Click on a patch to read the main article about that mission
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_7" title="Apollo 7">
        Apollo 7
       </a>
       , launched from LC-34 on October 11, 1968, was the C mission, crewed by Schirra, Eisele and Cunningham. It was an 11-day Earth-orbital flight which tested the CSM systems.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_8" title="Apollo 8">
        Apollo 8
       </a>
       was planned to be the D mission in December 1968, crewed by McDivitt, Scott and Schweickart, launched on a Saturn V instead of two Saturn IBs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the summer it had become clear that the LM would not be ready in time. Rather than waste the Saturn V on another simple Earth-orbiting mission, ASPO Manager George Low suggested the bold step of sending Apollo 8 to orbit the Moon instead, deferring the D mission to the next mission in March 1969, and eliminating the E mission. This would keep the program on track. The
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet Union
       </a>
       had sent two tortoises, mealworms, wine flies, and other lifeforms around the Moon on September 15, 1968, aboard
       <a href="/wiki/Zond_5" title="Zond 5">
        Zond 5
       </a>
       , and it was believed they might soon repeat the feat with human cosmonauts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chaikin_95-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Chaikin-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moon_Race_1968_96-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Moon_Race_1968-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The decision was not announced publicly until successful completion of Apollo 7. Gemini veterans
       <a href="/wiki/Frank_Borman" title="Frank Borman">
        Frank Borman
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Jim_Lovell" title="Jim Lovell">
        Jim Lovell
       </a>
       , and rookie
       <a href="/wiki/William_Anders" title="William Anders">
        William Anders
       </a>
       captured the world's attention by making ten lunar orbits in 20 hours, transmitting television pictures of the lunar surface on
       <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Eve" title="Christmas Eve">
        Christmas Eve
       </a>
       , and returning safely to Earth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The following March, LM flight, rendezvous and docking were successfully demonstrated in Earth orbit on
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_9" title="Apollo 9">
        Apollo 9
       </a>
       , and Schweickart tested the full lunar EVA suit with its
       <a href="/wiki/Primary_Life_Support_System" title="Primary Life Support System">
        Portable Life Support System
       </a>
       (PLSS) outside the LM.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The F mission was successfully carried out on
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_10" title="Apollo 10">
        Apollo 10
       </a>
       in May 1969 by Gemini veterans
       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_P._Stafford" title="Thomas P. Stafford">
        Thomas P. Stafford
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/John_Young_(astronaut)" title="John Young (astronaut)">
        John Young
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Eugene_Cernan" title="Eugene Cernan">
        Eugene Cernan
       </a>
       . Stafford and Cernan took the LM to within 50,000 feet (15 km) of the lunar surface.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_11_first_step.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="409" data-file-width="538" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Apollo_11_first_step.jpg/220px-Apollo_11_first_step.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Apollo_11_first_step.jpg/330px-Apollo_11_first_step.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Apollo_11_first_step.jpg/440px-Apollo_11_first_step.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_11_first_step.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Neil_Armstrong" title="Neil Armstrong">
          Neil Armstrong
         </a>
         descends the LM's ladder in preparation for the first steps on the lunar surface, as televised live on July 20, 1969
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The G mission was achieved on
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">
        Apollo 11
       </a>
       in July 1969 by an all-Gemini veteran crew consisting of Neil Armstrong, Michael Collins and Buzz Aldrin. Armstrong and Aldrin performed the first landing at the
       <a href="/wiki/Mare_Tranquillitatis" title="Mare Tranquillitatis">
        Sea of Tranquility
       </a>
       at 20:17:40
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">
        UTC
       </a>
       on July 20, 1969. They spent a total of 21 hours, 36 minutes on the surface, and spent 2 hours, 31 minutes outside the spacecraft,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statrefeva_100-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-statrefeva-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       walking on the surface, taking photographs, collecting material samples, and deploying automated scientific instruments, while continuously sending black-and-white television back to Earth. The astronauts returned safely on July 24.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        That's one small step for [a] man, one giant leap for mankind.
       </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>
         <a href="/wiki/Neil_Armstrong" title="Neil Armstrong">
          Neil Armstrong
         </a>
         , just after stepping onto the Moon's surface
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snopes_102-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Snopes-102">
           [102]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Production_lunar_landings">
        Production lunar landings
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Production lunar landings">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <div class="noresize">
         <map id="ImageMap_3_636230042" name="ImageMap_3_636230042">
          <area alt="Apollo 12 second manned Moon landing" coords="0,0,80,80" href="/wiki/Apollo_12" shape="rect" title="Apollo 12 second manned Moon landing"/>
          <area alt="Apollo 13 unsuccessful Moon landing attempt" coords="80,0,160,80" href="/wiki/Apollo_13" shape="rect" title="Apollo 13 unsuccessful Moon landing attempt"/>
          <area alt="Apollo 14 third manned Moon landing" coords="160,0,250,80" href="/wiki/Apollo_14" shape="rect" title="Apollo 14 third manned Moon landing"/>
          <area alt="Apollo 15 fourth manned Moon landing" coords="0,80,80,159" href="/wiki/Apollo_15" shape="rect" title="Apollo 15 fourth manned Moon landing"/>
          <area alt="Apollo 16 fifth manned Moon landing" coords="80,80,160,159" href="/wiki/Apollo_16" shape="rect" title="Apollo 16 fifth manned Moon landing"/>
          <area alt="Apollo 17 sixth manned Moon landing" coords="160,80,250,159" href="/wiki/Apollo_17" shape="rect" title="Apollo 17 sixth manned Moon landing"/>
         </map>
         <img alt="Composite image of 6 production manned Apollo lunar landing mission patches, from Apollo 12 to Apollo 17." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1885" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Apollo_lunar_landing_missions_insignia.png/250px-Apollo_lunar_landing_missions_insignia.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Apollo_lunar_landing_missions_insignia.png/375px-Apollo_lunar_landing_missions_insignia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Apollo_lunar_landing_missions_insignia.png/500px-Apollo_lunar_landing_missions_insignia.png 2x" usemap="#ImageMap_3_636230042" width="250"/>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_lunar_landing_missions_insignia.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Apollo production manned lunar landing mission patches. Click on a patch to read the main article about that mission
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_landing_sites.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2247" data-file-width="2364" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Apollo_landing_sites.jpg/220px-Apollo_landing_sites.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Apollo_landing_sites.jpg/330px-Apollo_landing_sites.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Apollo_landing_sites.jpg/440px-Apollo_landing_sites.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_landing_sites.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Apollo landings on the Moon, 1969–1972
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In November 1969, Gemini veteran
       <a href="/wiki/Pete_Conrad" title="Pete Conrad">
        Charles "Pete" Conrad
       </a>
       and rookie
       <a href="/wiki/Alan_Bean" title="Alan Bean">
        Alan L. Bean
       </a>
       made a precision landing on Apollo 12 within walking distance of the
       <a href="/wiki/Surveyor_3" title="Surveyor 3">
        Surveyor 3
       </a>
       unmanned lunar probe, which had landed in April 1967 on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ocean_of_Storms" title="Ocean of Storms">
        Ocean of Storms
       </a>
       . The Command Module Pilot was Gemini veteran
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_F._Gordon_Jr." title="Richard F. Gordon Jr.">
        Richard F. Gordon Jr.
       </a>
       Conrad and Bean carried the first lunar surface color television camera, but it was damaged when accidentally pointed into the Sun. They made two EVAs totaling 7 hours and 45 minutes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statrefeva_100-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-statrefeva-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On one, they walked to the Surveyor, photographed it, and removed some parts which they returned to Earth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The success of the first two landings allowed the remaining missions to be crewed with a single veteran as Commander, with two rookies. Apollo 13 launched Lovell,
       <a href="/wiki/Jack_Swigert" title="Jack Swigert">
        Jack Swigert
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Fred_Haise" title="Fred Haise">
        Fred Haise
       </a>
       in April 1970, headed for the
       <a href="/wiki/Fra_Mauro_formation" title="Fra Mauro formation">
        Fra Mauro formation
       </a>
       . But two days out, a liquid oxygen tank exploded, disabling the Service Module and forcing the crew to use the LM as a "life boat" to return to Earth. Another NASA review board was convened to determine the cause, which turned out to be a combination of damage of the tank in the factory, and a subcontractor not making a tank component according to updated design specifications.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KSC-Apollo_13_44-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-KSC-Apollo_13-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Apollo was grounded again, for the remainder of 1970 while the oxygen tank was redesigned and an extra one was added.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The contracted batch of 15 Saturn Vs were enough for lunar landing missions through Apollo 20. NASA publicized a preliminary list of eight more planned landing sites, with plans to increase the mass of the CSM and LM for the last five missions, along with the payload capacity of the Saturn V. These final missions would combine the I and J types in the 1967 list, allowing the CMP to operate a package of lunar orbital sensors and cameras while his companions were on the surface, and allowing them to stay on the Moon for over three days. These missions would also carry the
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Roving_Vehicle" title="Lunar Roving Vehicle">
        Lunar Roving Vehicle
       </a>
       (LRV) increasing the exploration area and allowing televised liftoff of the LM. Also, the Block II spacesuit was
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo/Skylab_A7L#A7LB_Spacesuit_(Apollo,_Skylab_and_ASTP)" title="Apollo/Skylab A7L">
        revised for the extended missions
       </a>
       to allow greater flexibility and visibility for driving the LRV.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_cutbacks">
        Mission cutbacks
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Mission cutbacks">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Canceled_Apollo_missions" title="Canceled Apollo missions">
        Canceled Apollo missions
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       About the time of the first landing in 1969, it was decided to use an existing Saturn V to launch the Skylab orbital laboratory pre-built on the ground, replacing the original plan to construct it in orbit from several Saturn IB launches; this eliminated Apollo 20. NASA's yearly budget also began to shrink in light of the successful landing, and NASA also had to make funds available for the development of the upcoming
       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">
        Space Shuttle
       </a>
       . By 1971, the decision was made to also cancel missions 18 and 19.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The two unused Saturn Vs became museum exhibits at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Space_Center" title="John F. Kennedy Space Center">
        John F. Kennedy Space Center
       </a>
       on Merritt Island, Florida,
       <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Space_Flight_Center" title="Marshall Space Flight Center">
        George C. Marshall Space Center
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Alabama" title="Huntsville, Alabama">
        Huntsville
       </a>
       , Alabama,
       <a href="/wiki/Michoud_Assembly_Facility" title="Michoud Assembly Facility">
        Michoud Assembly Facility
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">
        New Orleans
       </a>
       , Louisiana, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson_Space_Center" title="Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center">
        Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center
       </a>
       in Houston, Texas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The cutbacks forced mission planners to reassess the original planned landing sites in order to achieve the most effective geological sample and data collection from the remaining four missions.
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_15" title="Apollo 15">
        Apollo 15
       </a>
       had been planned to be the last of the H series missions, but since there would be only two subsequent missions left, it was changed to the first of three J missions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Apollo 13's Fra Mauro mission was reassigned to
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_14" title="Apollo 14">
        Apollo 14
       </a>
       , commanded in February 1971 by Mercury veteran
       <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shepard" title="Alan Shepard">
        Alan Shepard
       </a>
       , with
       <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Roosa" title="Stuart Roosa">
        Stuart Roosa
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Mitchell" title="Edgar Mitchell">
        Edgar Mitchell
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apollo14_109-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-apollo14-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This time the mission was successful. Shepard and Mitchell spent 33 hours and 31 minutes on the surface,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and completed two EVAs totalling 9 hours 24 minutes, which was a record for the longest EVA by a lunar crew at the time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apollo14_109-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-apollo14-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In August 1971, just after conclusion of the Apollo 15 mission, President
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">
        Richard Nixon
       </a>
       proposed canceling the two remaining lunar landing missions, Apollo 16 and 17.
